[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

### ROUND: Round numerical value (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Round numerical value" instruction to round the value at input IN to the nearest integer. The instruction interprets the value at input IN as a floating-point number and converts this to an integer of data type DINT. If the input value is exactly between an even and odd number, the even number is selected. The result of the instruction is sent to the OUT output and can be queried there.

Enable output ENO has signal state "0" if one of the following conditions applies:

- Enable input EN has signal state "0".
- Errors, such as an overflow, occur during execution.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Round numerical value" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Input value to be rounded. |
| OUT | Output | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of rounding |

You can select the data type for the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20115469067_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | 1.50000000 | -1.50000000 |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | 2 | -2 |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The floating-point number at input "TagIn_Value" is rounded to the nearest even integer and sent to output "TagOut_Value". If the instruction is executed without errors, the "TagOut" output is set.

---

### CEIL: Generate next higher integer from floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Generate next higher integer from floating-point number" instruction to round the value at input IN to the next higher integer. The instruction interprets the value at the IN input as a floating-point number and converts this number to the next higher integer. The result of the instruction is sent to the OUT output and can be queried there. The output value can be greater than or equal to the input value.

Enable output ENO has signal state "0" if one of the following conditions applies:

- Enable input EN has signal state "0".
- Errors, such as an overflow, occur during execution.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Generate next higher integer from floating-point number" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | Floating-point numbers | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Input value |
| OUT | Output | Integers, floating-point numbers | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result with next higher integer |

You can select the data type for the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20115826315_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | 0.50000000 | -0.50000000 |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | 1 | 0 |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The floating-point number at the "TagIn_Value" input is rounded to the next higher integer and sent to the "TagOut_Value" output. If the instruction is executed without errors, the "TagOut" output is set.

### FLOOR: Generate next lower integer from floating-point number (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Generate next lower integer from floating-point number" instruction to round the value at input IN to the next lower integer. The instruction interprets the value at input IN as a floating-point number and converts this to the next lower integer. The result of the instruction is sent to the OUT output and can be queried there. The output value can be less than or equal to the input value.

Enable output ENO has signal state "0" if one of the following conditions applies:

- Enable input EN has signal state "0".
- Errors, such as an overflow, occur during execution.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Generate next lower integer from floating-point number" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | Floating-point numbers | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Input value |
| OUT | Output | Integers, floating-point numbers | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result with next lower integer |

You can select the data type for the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20115890059_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | 0.50000000 | -0.50000000 |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | 0 | -1 |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The floating-point number at input "TagIn_Value" is rounded to the next lower integer and sent to output "TagOut_Value". If the instruction is executed without errors, the "TagOut" output is set.

### TRUNC: Truncate numerical value (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Truncate numerical value" instruction to form an integer from the value at the IN input. The value at the IN input is interpreted as a floating-point number. The instruction selects only the integer part of the floating-point number and sends this to the OUT output without decimal places.

Enable output ENO has signal state "0" if one of the following conditions applies:

- Enable input EN has signal state "0".
- Errors, such as an overflow, occur during execution.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Truncate numerical value" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Input value |
| OUT | Output | Integers | I, Q, M, D, L | Integer part of the input value |

You can select the data type for the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20115979403_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | 1.50000000 | -1.50000000 |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | 1 | -1 |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The integer part of the floating-point number at the "TagIn_Value" input is converted to an integer and sent to the "TagOut_Value" output. If the instruction is executed without errors, the "TagOut" output is set.

### SCALE: Scale (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

Use the "Scale" instruction to convert the integer at the IN parameter into a floating-point number, which can be scaled in physical units between a low limit and a high limit. You can use the LO_LIM and HI_LIM parameters to specify the low limit and high limit of the value range to which the input value is scaled. The result of the instruction is output at the OUT parameter.

The "Scale" instruction works with the following equation:

OUT = [((FLOAT (IN) – K1)/(K2–K1)) ∗ (HI_LIM–LO_LIM)] + LO_LIM

The values of the constants "K1" and "K2" are determined by the signal state of the BIPOLAR parameter. The following signal states are possible at the BIPOLAR parameter:

- Signal state "1": It is assumed that the value at the IN parameter is bipolar and in a value range between -27648 and 27648. In this case the "K1" constant has the value "-27648.0" and the "K2" constant the value "+27648.0".
- Signal state "0": It is assumed that the value at the IN parameter is unipolar and in a value range between 0 and 27648. In this case the "K1" constant has the value "0.0" and the "K2" constant the value "+27648.0".

When the value at the IN parameter is greater than the value of the constant "K2", the result of the instruction is set to the value of the high limit (HI_LIM) and an error is output.

When the value at the IN parameter is less than the value of the constant "K1", the result of the instruction is set to the value of the low limit (LO_LIM) and an error is output.

When the indicated low limit is greater than the high limit (LO_LIM &gt; HI_LIM), the result is scaled in reverse proportion to the input value.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Scale" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Input value to be scaled |
| HI_LIM | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | High limit |
| LO_LIM | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Low limit |
| BIPOLAR | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Indicates if the value at the IN parameter is to be interpreted as bipolar or unipolar. The parameter can assume the following values:  1: Bipolar  0: Unipolar |
| OUT | Output | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |
| RET_VAL | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |

#### RET_VAL parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 0008 | The value of the IN parameter is greater than the value of the constant "K2" or less than the value of the constant "K1" |
| 8xyy | For more information on errors, refer to "See also". |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For additional information on switching display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/11637048971_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_InputValue | 22 |
| HI_LIM | Tag_HighLimit | 100.0 |
| LO_LIM | Tag_LowLimit | 0.0 |
| BIPOLAR | Tag_Bipolar | 1 |
| OUT | Tag_OutputValue | 50.03978588 |
| RET_VAL | Tag_ErrorCode | W#16#0000 |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

### UNSCALE: Unscale (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use the "Unscale" instruction to unscale the floating-point number in the IN parameter into physical units between a low limit and a high limit and convert it into an integer. You use the LO_LIM and HI_LIM parameters to specify the low limit and high limit of the value range to which the input value is unscaled. The result of the instruction is output at the OUT parameter.

The "Unscale" instruction works with the following equation:

OUT = [ ((IN–LO_LIM)/(HI_LIM–LO_LIM)) ∗ (K2–K1) ] + K1

The values of the "K1" and "K2" constants are determined by the signal state at the BIPOLAR parameter. The following signal states are possible at the BIPOLAR parameter:

- Signal state "1": It is assumed that the value at the IN parameter is bipolar and in a value range between -27648 and 27648. In this case the "K1" constant has the value "-27648.0" and the "K2" constant the value "+27648.0".
- Signal state "0": It is assumed that the value at the IN parameter is unipolar and in a value range between 0 and 27648. In this case the "K1" constant has the value "0.0" and the "K2" constant the value "+27648.0".

When the value at parameter IN is not within the limits defined by HI_LIM and LO_LIM, an error is output and the result is set to the nearest limit.

When the indicated low limit value is greater than the high limit value (LO_LIM &gt; HI_LIM), the result is scaled in reverse proportion to the input value.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Unscale" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Input value to be unscaled to an integer value |
| HI_LIM | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | High limit |
| LO_LIM | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Low limit |
| BIPOLAR | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Indicates whether the value at the IN parameter is to be interpreted as bipolar or unipolar. The parameter can assume the following values:  1: Bipolar  0: Unipolar |
| OUT | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |
| RET_VAL | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |

#### RET_VAL parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 0008 | The value of the IN parameter is greater than the value of the high limit (HI_LIM) or less than the value of the low limit (LO_LIM). |
| 8xyy | For additional information on errors, refer to "See also". |
| * The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal values in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats here: [Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status) |  |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/50929795083_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_InputValue | 50.03978588 |
| HI_LIM | Tag_HighLimit | 100.0 |
| LO_LIM | Tag_LowLimit | 0.0 |
| BIPOLAR | Tag_Bipolar | 1 |
| OUT | Tag_OutputValue | 22 |
| RET_VAL | Tag_ErrorCode | W#16#0000 |

---

## Program control operations (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [---( JMP ): Jump if RLO = 1 (S7-300, S7-400)](#jmp-jump-if-rlo-1-s7-300-s7-400)
- [---( JMPN ): Jump if RLO = 0 (S7-300, S7-400)](#jmpn-jump-if-rlo-0-s7-300-s7-400)
- [LABEL: Jump label (S7-300, S7-400)](#label-jump-label-s7-300-s7-400)
- [--(RET): Return (S7-300, S7-400)](#ret-return-s7-300-s7-400)
- [---(OPN): Open global data block (S7-300, S7-400)](#opn-open-global-data-block-s7-300-s7-400)
- [---(OPNI): Open instance data block (S7-300, S7-400)](#opni-open-instance-data-block-s7-300-s7-400)
- [Runtime control (S7-300, S7-400)](#runtime-control-s7-300-s7-400)

### ---( JMP ): Jump if RLO = 1 (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Jump if RLO = 1" instruction to interrupt the linear execution of the program and resume it in another network. The destination network must be identified by a jump label (LABEL). The name of this jump label is specified in the placeholder above the instruction.

The specified jump label must be in the same block in which the instruction is executed. The name you specify can only occur once in the block. Only one jumping coil is permitted within a network.

If the result of logic operation (RLO) at the input of the instruction is "1", the jump to the network identified by the specified jump label is executed. The jump direction can be towards higher or lower network numbers.

If the condition at the input of the instruction is not fulfilled (RLO = 0), execution of the program continues in the next network.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20126444555_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

If operand "TagIn_1" has the signal state "1", the "Jump if RLO = 1" instruction is executed. The linear execution of the program is interrupted and continues in Network 3, which is identified by the jump label CAS1. If the "TagIn_3" input has signal state "1", the "TagOut_3" output is set.

---

**See also**

[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)

### ---( JMPN ): Jump if RLO = 0 (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the instruction "Jump if RLO = 0" to interrupt the linear execution of the program and resume it in another network, when the result of logic operation at the input of the instruction is "0". The destination network must be identified by a jump label (LABEL). The name of this jump label is specified in the placeholder above the instruction.

The specified jump label must be in the same block in which the instruction is executed. The name you specify can only occur once in the block. Only one jumping coil is permitted within a network.

If the result of logic operation (RLO) at the input of the instruction is "0", the jump to the network identified by the specified jump label is executed. The jump direction can be towards higher or lower network numbers.

If the result of logic operation at the input of the instruction is "1", execution of the program continues in the next network.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20127062539_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

If operand "TagIn_1" has the signal state "0", the "Jump if RLO = 0" instruction is executed. The linear execution of the program is interrupted and continues in Network 3, which is identified by the jump label CAS1. If the "TagIn_3" input has signal state "1", the "TagOut_3" output is set.

---

**See also**

[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)

### LABEL: Jump label (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use a jump label to identify a destination network, in which the program execution should resume when a jump is executed.

The jump label and the instruction in which the jump label is specified must be located in the same block. The name of a jump label can only be assigned once in a block.

Only one jump label can be placed in a network. Each jump label can jump to several locations.

The following grammar rules must be followed for the jump label:

- Letters (a - z, A - Z)
- A combination of letters and numbers. Check that the order is correct, i.e. first the letters, then the numbers (a - z, A - Z, 0 - 9).
- Special characters or a combination of letters and numbers in reverse order, i.e. first the numbers and then the letters (0-9, a - z, A - Z), must not be used.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20127168523_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

If operand "TagIn_1" has the signal state "1", the "Jump if RLO = 1" instruction is executed. The linear execution of the program is interrupted and continues in Network 3, which is identified by the jump label CAS1. If the "TagIn_3" input has signal state "1", the "TagOut_3" output is set.

---

**See also**

[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)

### --(RET): Return (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use the "Return" instruction to end the execution of a program block.

- If the result of logic operation (RLO) at the input of the "Return" instruction is "1", the program execution is ended in the currently called program block and continued after the call function in the calling program block (for example, in the calling organization block). The signal state of the enable output ENO of the call function is determined by the RLO. The RLO is displayed as a fixed parameter value above the instruction.
- If the result of logic operation (RLO) at the input of the instruction is "0", then the instruction will not be executed. The program execution is continued in the next network of the called program block.

If the instruction is programmed in the last network of the called block, the enable output ENO of the call function is set to the current signal state of the RLO.

If an organization block is ended with the instruction, the CPU goes on working in the system program.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/22497269899_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the "TagIn" operand returns signal state "1", the instruction is executed. Program execution is ended in the called program block and continues in the calling program block. The ENO enable output of the call function is set to signal state "1".

---

**See also**

[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)

### ---(OPN): Open global data block (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Open global data block" instruction to open a global data block (DB). The number of the data block is transferred to the DB register. Subsequent DB commands access the relevant blocks depending on the content of the register.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Open global data block" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Data block&gt; | Input | DB_ANY | DB | Data block to be opened. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/26300012299_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

The "Motor_DB" data block is called in network 1. The number of the data block is transferred to the DB register. The "DBX0.0" operand is queried in network 2. The signal state of the DBX0.0 operand is assigned to the Tag_Output operand.

---

[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)

### ---(OPNI): Open instance data block (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Open instance data block" instruction to open a data block (DB). The number of the data block is transferred to the DI register. Subsequent DI commands access the relevant blocks depending on the content of the register.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Open instance data block" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Data block&gt; | Input | DB_ANY | DB | Data block to be opened |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/26300722571_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

The "Motor_DB" data block is called in network 1. The number of the data block is transferred to the DI register. The "DBX0.0" operand is queried in network 2. The signal state of the DBX0.0 operand is assigned to the Tag_Output operand.

---

### Runtime control (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [COMPRESS: Compress CPU memory (S7-400)](#compress-compress-cpu-memory-s7-400)
- [RE_TRIGR: Restart cycle monitoring time (S7-300, S7-400)](#re_trigr-restart-cycle-monitoring-time-s7-300-s7-400)
- [STP: Exit program (S7-300, S7-400)](#stp-exit-program-s7-300-s7-400)
- [WAIT: Configure time delay (S7-300, S7-400)](#wait-configure-time-delay-s7-300-s7-400)
- [PROTECT: Change protection level (S7-300, S7-400)](#protect-change-protection-level-s7-300-s7-400)
- [CiR: Control CiR process (S7-400)](#cir-control-cir-process-s7-400)

#### COMPRESS: Compress CPU memory (S7-400)

##### Description

The "Compress CPU memory" instruction is used to compress the working memory of the CPU or the RAM work memory. During this compression the gaps caused by deleting or loading blocks are filled by pushing together the existing blocks.

The compression operation is started by calling the "Compress CPU memory" instruction. The compression operation is divided into several program cycles. The compression operation is monitored by the values of the individual parameters. If value "1" is on the BUSY parameter of the instruction, the compression operation is still being executed. The value "1" on the DONE parameter reports that the compression operation has been completed. Error information can be queried on the RET_VAL parameter.

If an externally started compression operation has already been executed, the calling of the "Compress CPU memory" instruction causes an error to be displayed.

##### Parameter

The following table shows the parameters of the "Compress CPU memory" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | Error information:  If an error occurs during execution of the instruction, an error code is output on the RET_VAL parameter. |
| BUSY | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Information whether compression operation is active. |
| DONE | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Information whether compression operation was completed. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

##### Parameter RET_VAL

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error  The status of the compression operation can be queried on the BUSY and DONE parameters. |
| 8091 | An externally started compression operation is already being executed. |
| 8092 | The operation cannot be executed, because one of the following conditions applies:  - The "Delete block" function is active. - A test and commissioning function affects a block (for  example, status). - The "copy blocks" function was triggered externally and is active. - The H-CPU is running a link-up or update function. |
| 8xyy | For more information on errors, refer to "See also". |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For additional information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

---

**See also**

[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

#### RE_TRIGR: Restart cycle monitoring time (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

The "Restart cycle monitoring time" instruction is used to restart the cycle monitoring time of the CPU. The cycle monitoring time then restarts with the time you have set in the CPU configuration.

The instruction "Restart cycle monitoring time" can be called in all blocks regardless of the priority .

If the instruction is called in a block with a higher priority, for example a hardware interrupt or a diagnostics interrupt, the instruction is not executed and the enable output ENO is set to signal state "0".

The "Restart cycle monitoring time" instruction executes completely within a time span (10 times the maximum program cycle), regardless of the number of calls. Once this time has expired, the program cycle can no longer be prolonged.

##### Parameters

The instruction "Restart cycle monitoring time" has no parameters.

---

**See also**

[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

#### STP: Exit program (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

You use the "Exit program" instruction to set the CPU to STOP mode and thus end the program execution. The effects at a transition from RUN to STOP depend on the CPU configuration.

When the result of logic operation (RLO) at the input of the instruction is "1", the CPU changes to STOP mode and the program execution is ended. The signal state at the output of the instruction is not evaluated.

When the RLO is "0" at the input of the instruction, then the instruction will not be executed.

##### Parameters

The "Exit program" instruction has no parameters.

---

**See also**

[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

#### WAIT: Configure time delay (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

The "Configure time delay" instruction pauses the program execution for a specific period of time. You indicate the period of time in microseconds on the WT parameter of the instruction.

You can configure time delays from -32768 up to 32767 microseconds (μs). The smallest possible delay time depends on the CPU and corresponds to the execution time of the instruction.

The execution of the instruction can be interrupted by higher priority events and does not return any error information.

Applies to S7-300-CPUs:

For the S7-300-CPUs (except S7-318), the delay time programmed by the instruction is a minimum time. It is extended by the execution time of the nested priority classes and by system utilizations.

> **Note**
>
> **Negative delay time**
>
> If you specify a negative delay time at parameter WT, the enable output ENO, or the RLO and the BR bit, will return the signal state FALSE. A negative delay time does not affect the CPU. The following instructions linked to enable output ENO are not executed in LAD or FBD.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Configure time delay" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| WT | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Time delay in microseconds (μs) |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basics of the EN/ENO mechanism](Programming%20basics.md#basics-of-the-eneno-mechanism)
  
[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

#### PROTECT: Change protection level (S7-300, S7-400)

##### Description

The instruction "Change protection level" is used to change the configured protection level "1" of the CPU.

The configured protection level "1" with selected option "Removable with password", means that you have to configure a password. This password enables you to write-access during operation the CPU which was read-only protected with the instruction "Change Protection Level" (e. g. Load).

You specify the protection level on the MODE parameter of the instruction. The current protection level of your CPU is displayed in the inspector window under "Properties &gt; Protection".

The following table shows the meaning of the protection levels.

| Protection level | Meaning |
| --- | --- |
| 1 | All programming device functions are permitted. Any existing blocking of the password authentication is canceled by the instruction "Change protection level". |
| 2 | - The program and the configuration of the CPU cannot be changed. The program in the CPU can be read. - The functions for process control, process monitoring, and process communication are permitted. - All informational functions are permitted. - If you know the valid password you can cancel the set write protection. - Any existing blocking of the password authentication is canceled by the instruction "Change protection level". |
| 3 | - You cannot cancel the set read and write protection, even if you know the valid password. - If a valid connection exists at the time when the instruction "Change protection level" is called, the call of the instruction does not affect this connection. |

If you have configured protection level "2" or "3" for your CPU, calling the "Change protection level" instruction has no effect.

You can use the SSL parts list with the SSL ID W#16#0232 and index W#16#0004 to check whether protection level "2" or "3" is still in effect after the execution of the "Change protection level" instruction.

> **Note**
>
> You can only use the "Change protection level" instruction to set a protection level that is equal to or higher than the protection level you have configured with STEP 7 "Configure hardware. You have, for example, configured protection level 3 and then called the instruction "Change protection level" with the MODE parameter = 12. This blocks the password authentication. If the instruction is called again with the parameter MODE = 0 or 1, protection level 3 is retained and the read and write protection canceled by entry of the valid password.

##### Effects of the operating state transitions on the protection level

The following table shows what effects the operating state transitions have on the protection level set with the "Change protection level" instruction.

| Action | Effects on the protection level |
| --- | --- |
| - Operating mode switch to "STOP" - Unbuffered POWER ON - Memory reset with operating mode switch - Configuration and/or programming changes in the "STOP" mode of the S7-400 CPU | The protection level is set to "1". All programming device functions are permitted. |
| - Cold restart - Warm restart | The protection level is set by the operating system to "1". All programming device functions are permitted.  If required, you can set the protection level in your program to "2" or "3" by calling the "Change protection level" instruction. |
| Buffered POWER ON | Remains unchanged |
| Operating mode change RUN/STARTUP/HOLD -&gt; STOP (by calling the instruction "Exit program" (STP), due to a program error without corresponding error OB or by an operator action). | Remains unchanged |
| S7-400: Restart by user action or automatically following POWER ON | Remains unchanged |

##### Parameter

The following table shows the parameters of the "Change protection level" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| MODE | Input | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Protection level  Possible values:  - W#16#0000: Setting protection level "1" - W#16#0001: Setting protection level "2" with password authentication - W#16#000C: Setting protection level "3" with password authentication   Constants can also be specified on the MODE parameter. |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | If an error occurs during processing, information on the error is output. |

##### Parameter RET_VAL

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | Job executed without error |
| 8090 | Invalid value at parameter MODE. |
| 80C3 | The required operating resources are currently occupied. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For additional information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basics of the EN/ENO mechanism](Programming%20basics.md#basics-of-the-eneno-mechanism)
  
[Switching display formats in the program status](Testing%20the%20user%20program.md#switching-display-formats-in-the-program-status)
  
[Evaluating errors with output parameter RET_VAL](Programming%20basics.md#evaluating-errors-with-output-parameter-ret_val)
  
[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

#### CiR: Control CiR process (S7-400)

##### Description

The "Control CiR process" instruction is used to influence the CiR process in the user program as follows:

- Disable CiR process. In this case, the download of a modified configuration from the programming device to the CPU is always rejected. The disable is maintained until you cancel it again with the "Control CiR process" instruction.
- You can disable the CiR process conditionally by specifying a high limit for the CiR synchronization time on the FRZ_TIME parameter. In this case, the download of a modified configuration from the programming device to the CPU is only accepted if the CiR synchronization time calculated in the CPU does not exceed the specified high limit.
- Disable CiR process. The high limit of the CiR synchronization time is set to the default value 1000 ms.
- Determine whether the CiR process is enabled or not. If the CiR process is enabled or conditionally enabled, you will get the current high limit for the CiR synchronization time in the A_FT parameter of the instruction.

  > **Note**
  >
  > During the CiR synchronization period the outputs are frozen and the inputs are not evaluated.

##### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Control CiR process" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| MODE | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Job identifier  Valid values on the MODE parameter are:  - 0: Information function - 1: Enable CiR process - 2: Disable CiR process - 3: Disable CiR conditionally. You specify the high limit of the CiR synchronization time in FRZ_TIME. |
| FRZ_TIME | Input | TIME | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | High limit of the CiR synchronization time in milliseconds.   Permitted range of values: 60 ... 2500 ms (default: 1000 ms)  The FRZ_TIME parameter is only relevant when the value 3 is set on the MODE parameter. |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | Error information  When the MODE parameter is "0", the RET_VAL parameter supplies information on the enabling of the CiR process. |
| A_FT | Output | TIME | I, Q, M, D, L | Currently valid high limit of the CiR synchronization time |

##### Parameter RET_VAL

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | Job executed without error  This error code can be output only if the value "1", "2" or "3" is set on the MODE parameter. |
| 0001 | CiR is enabled.  This error code can be output only if the value "0" is set on the MODE parameter. |
| 0002 | The CiR process is disabled.  This error code can be output only if the value "0" is set on the MODE parameter. |
| 0003 | CiR is disabled conditionally.  This error code can be output only if the value "0" is set on the MODE parameter. |
| 8001 | The CPU is not ready for a CiR operation. You are using an H CPU in an H-system (stand-alone), or you are working with a standard CPU in multicomputing mode. |
| 8002 | The value at the MODE parameter is invalid. |
| 8003 | The value at the FRZ_TIME parameter is invalid. |
| 8xyy | For more information on errors, refer to "See also". |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For additional information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

##### Example

The "Control CiR process" instruction can be used, for example, to ensure that no CiR process is initiated during periods in which maximum CPU performance is required for the execution of the process.

To use the "Control CiR process" for this, the instruction must be called before the start of the period with increased process activity and executed with the value "2" (disable CiR process) on the MODE parameter. The CiR process is then disabled.

To enable the CiR process again after the completion of the period with increased process activity, you have to again call the "Control CiR process" instruction and execute it with the value "1" on the MODE parameter. Alternatively, you can also set the value 3 on the MODE parameter to disable the CiR process conditionally.

---

## Word logic operations (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [AND: AND logic operation (S7-300, S7-400)](#and-and-logic-operation-s7-300-s7-400)
- [OR: OR logic operation (S7-300, S7-400)](#or-or-logic-operation-s7-300-s7-400)
- [XOR: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation (S7-300, S7-400)](#xor-exclusive-or-logic-operation-s7-300-s7-400)
- [INVERT: Create ones complement (S7-300, S7-400)](#invert-create-ones-complement-s7-300-s7-400)
- [DECO: Decode (S7-300, S7-400)](#deco-decode-s7-300-s7-400)
- [ENCO: Encode (S7-300, S7-400)](#enco-encode-s7-300-s7-400)
- [SEL: Select (S7-300, S7-400)](#sel-select-s7-300-s7-400)

### AND: AND logic operation (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "AND logic operation" instruction to combine the value at the IN1 input and the value at the IN2 input bit-by-bit by AND logic and query the result at the OUT output.

When the instruction is executed, bit 0 of the value at the IN1 input and bit 0 of the value at the IN2 input are logically ANDed. The result is stored in bit 0 of output OUT. The same logic operation is executed for all other bits of the specified values.

The result bit has signal state "1" only when both of the bits in the logic operation also have signal state "1". If one of the two bits of the logic operation has signal state "0", the corresponding result bit is reset.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "AND logic operation" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN1 | Input | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | First value for logic operation |
| IN2 | Input | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Second value for logic operation |
| OUT | Output | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |

You can select the data type of the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20534204043_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN1 | Tag_Value1 | 0101 0101 0101 0101 |
| IN2 | Tag_Value2 | 0000 0000 0000 1111 |
| OUT | Tag_Result | 0000 0000 0000 0101 |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The value of operand "Tag_Value1" and the value of operand "Tag_Value2" are ANDed. The result is mapped bit-for-bit and output in operand "Tag_Result". The enable output ENO and the output "TagOut" are set to signal state "1".

### OR: OR logic operation (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "OR logic operation" instruction to combine the value at the IN1 input and the value at the IN2 input bit-by-bit by OR logic and query the result at the OUT output.

When the instruction is executed, bit 0 of the value at the IN1 input and bit 0 of the value at the IN2 input are combined by OR logic operation. The result is stored in bit 0 of output OUT. The same logic operation is executed for all bits of the specified tags.

The result bit has signal state "1" when at least one of the two bits in the logic operation has signal state "1". If both of the bits of the logic operation have signal state "0", the corresponding result bit is reset.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "OR logic operation" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN1 | Input | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | First value for logic operation |
| IN2 | Input | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Second value for logic operation |
| OUT | Output | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |

You can select the data type of the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20535880331_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN1 | Tag_Value1 | 0101 0101 0101 0101 |
| IN2 | Tag_Value2 | 0000 0000 0000 1111 |
| OUT | Tag_Result | 0101 0101 0101 1111 |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The value of operand "Tag_Value1" and the value of operand "Tag_Value2" are ‏ORed. The result is mapped bit-for-bit and output in operand "Tag_Result". The enable output ENO and the output "TagOut" are set to signal state "1".

### XOR: EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation" instruction to combine the value at the IN1 input and the value at the IN2 input bit-by-bit by EXCLUSIVE OR logic and query the result at the OUT output.

When the instruction is executed, bit 0 of the value at the IN1 input and bit 0 of the value at the IN2 input are combined by EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation. The result is stored in bit 0 of output OUT. The same logic operation is executed for all other bits of the specified value.

The result bit has signal state "1" when one of the two bits in the logic operation has signal state "1". If both of the bits of the logic operation have signal state "1" or "0", the corresponding result bit is reset.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "EXCLUSIVE OR logic operation" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN1 | Input | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | First value for logic operation |
| IN2 | Input | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Second value for logic operation |
| OUT | Output | WORD, DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |

You can select the data type of the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20535905419_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN1 | Tag_Value1 | 0101 0101 0101 0101 |
| IN2 | Tag_Value2 | 0000 0000 0000 1111 |
| OUT | Tag_Result | 0101 0101 0101 1010 |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The value of operand "Tag_Value1" and the value of operand "Tag_Value2" are combined by EXCLUSIVE OR logic. The result is mapped bit-for-bit and output in operand "Tag_Result". The enable output ENO and the output "TagOut" are set to signal state "1".

### INVERT: Create ones complement (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the instruction "Create ones complement" to invert the signal status of the bits at input IN. When the instruction is processed, the value at the IN input and a hexadecimal template (W#16#FFFF for 16-bit numbers or DW#16#FFFFFFFF for 32-bit numbers) are combined by EXCLUSIVE OR logic. This inverts the signal state of the individual bits that are then stored at output OUT.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the instruction "Create ones complement":

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | Integers | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Input value |
| OUT | Output | Integers | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Ones complement of the value at input IN |

You can select the data type of the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/21380245771_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | W#16#000F |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | W#16#FFF0 |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The instruction inverts the signal state of the individual bits at input "TagIn_Value" and writes the result to output "TagOut_Value". The enable output ENO and the output "TagOut" are set to signal state "1".

---

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

### DECO: Decode (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Decode" instruction to set a bit in the output value that is specified by the input value.

The "Decode" instruction reads the value at the IN input and sets the bit in the output value whose bit position corresponds to the read value. The other bits in the output value are filled with zeroes. When the value at input IN is greater than 31, a modulo 32 instruction is executed.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Decode" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Position of the bit in the output value which is set. |
| OUT | Output | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Output value |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/41942779403_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following figure shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

![Example](images/51492952331_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The instruction reads bit number "3" from the value of the operand "TagIn_Value" at the input and sets the third bit to the value of the operand "TagOut_Value" at the output.

If the instruction is executed without errors, the ENO enable output has signal state "1" and the "TagOut" output is set.

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basics of the EN/ENO mechanism](Programming%20basics.md#basics-of-the-eneno-mechanism)

### ENCO: Encode (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

Use the "Encode" instruction to read the bit number of the least significant bit in the input value and to send it to the output OUT.

The "Encode" instruction selects the least significant bit of the value at the IN input and writes its bit number to the tag in the OUT output. If the IN input has the value DW#16#00000001 or DW#16#00000000, the value "0" is output at the OUT output.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Encode" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Input value |
| OUT | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Output value |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20536327563_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following figure shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

![Example](images/51493670539_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. The instruction selects the least significant bit at the "TagIn_Value" input and writes bit position "3" to the tag in the "TagOut_Value" output.

If the instruction is executed without errors, the ENO enable output has signal state "1" and the "TagOut" output is set.

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basics of the EN/ENO mechanism](Programming%20basics.md#basics-of-the-eneno-mechanism)

[Basic information on LAD](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#basic-information-on-lad)
  
[Memory areas (S7-300, S7-400)](Functional%20description%20of%20S7-300-400%20CPUs%20%28S7-300%2C%20S7-400%29.md#memory-areas-s7-300-s7-400)

### SEL: Select (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use the "Select" instruction to select, dependent on a switch (G input) one of two inputs, IN0 or IN1, and move its content to the OUT output. If the G input has signal state "0", the value at the IN0 input is moved. If the G input has the signal state "1", the value of the IN1 input is moved to the OUT output.

The instruction is only executed if the tags of all parameters have the same data type.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Select" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| G | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Switch |
| IN0 | Input | Bit strings, integers, floating-point numbers, timers, CHAR, TOD, DATE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | First input value |
| IN1 | Input | Bit strings, integers, floating-point numbers, timers, CHAR, TOD, DATE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Second input value |
| OUT | Output | Bit strings, integers, floating-point numbers, timers, CHAR, TOD, DATE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result |

You can select the data type of the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

> **Note**
>
> **Parameter assignment**
>
> In addition, input parameters (Input), output parameters (Output) and in/out parameters (InOut) of functions must not be connected to the input and output parameters of the instruction. If required, use a temporary tag (Temp) as buffer.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/25887311499_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| G | TagIn_G | 0 | 1 |
| IN0 | TagIn_Value0 | W#16#0000 | W#16#4C |
| IN1 | TagIn_Value1 | W#16#FFFF | W#16#5E |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | W#16#0000 | W#16#5E |

If the "TagIn" operand has signal state "1", the instruction is executed. Based on the signal state at the "TagIn_G" input, the value at the "TagIn_Value0" or "TagIn_Value1" input is selected and moved to the "TagOut_Value" output. f the instruction is executed without errors, the enable output ENO has the signal state "1" and the "TagOut" output is set.

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

## Shift and rotate (S7-300, S7-400)

This section contains information on the following topics:

- [SHR: Shift right (S7-300, S7-400)](#shr-shift-right-s7-300-s7-400)
- [SHL: Shift left (S7-300, S7-400)](#shl-shift-left-s7-300-s7-400)
- [ROR: Rotate right (S7-300, S7-400)](#ror-rotate-right-s7-300-s7-400)
- [ROL: Rotate left (S7-300, S7-400)](#rol-rotate-left-s7-300-s7-400)

### SHR: Shift right (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Shift right" instruction to shift the content of the operand at the IN input bit-by-bit to the right and query the result at the OUT output. You use the N parameter to specify the number of bit positions by which the specified value is to be shifted.

If the value at the parameter N is "0", the value at input IN is copied to the operand at output OUT.

If the value at the parameter N is greater than the number of bit positions, the operand value at input IN is shifted to the right by the available number of bit positions.

The freed bit positions in the left area of the operand are filled by zeroes when values without signs are shifted. If the specified value has a sign, the free bit positions are filled with the signal state of the sign bit.

The following figure shows how the content of an operand of the INT data type is shifted by four bit positions to the right:

![Description](images/51494437131_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Shift right" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | BYTE, WORD, DWORD, INT, DINT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Value to be shifted. |
| N | Input | BYTE, WORD, INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Number of bit positions by which the value is shifted. |
| OUT | Output | BYTE, WORD, DWORD, INT, DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Result of the instruction |

You can select the data type of the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20547202059_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | 0011 1111 1010 1111 |
| N | Tag_Number | 3 |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | 0000 0111 1111 0101 |

If operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the "Shift right" instruction is executed. The content of the operand "TagIn_Value" is shifted three bit positions to the right. The result is sent to the "TagOut_Value" output. If the instruction is executed without errors, the ENO enable output has the signal state "1" and the "TagOut" output is set.

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

### SHL: Shift left (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Shift left" instruction to shift the content of the operand at the IN input bit-by-bit to the left and query the result at the OUT output. You use the N parameter to specify the number of bit positions by which the specified value is to be shifted.

If the value at the parameter N is "0", the value at input IN is copied to the operand at output OUT.

If the value at the parameter N is greater than the number of bit positions, the operand value at input IN is shifted to the right by the available number of bit positions.

The bit positions in the right part of the operand freed by shifting are filled with zeros.

The following figure shows how the content of an operand of the WORD data type is shifted by six bit positions to the left:

![Description](images/51495651851_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Shift left" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | BYTE, WORD, DWORD, INT, DINT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Value to be shifted |
| N | Input | BYTE, WORD, INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Number of bit positions by which the value is shifted |
| OUT | Output | BYTE, WORD, DWORD, INT, DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Result of the instruction |

You can select the data type of the instruction from the "???" drop-down list of the instruction box.

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20547308427_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | 0011 1111 1010 1111 |
| N | Tag_Number | 4 |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | 1111 1010 1111 0000 |

If operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the "Shift left" instruction is executed. The content of the operand "TagIn_Value" is shifted four bit positions to the left. The result is sent at the "TagOut_Value" output. If the instruction is executed without errors, the ENO enable output has the signal state "1" and the "TagOut" output is set.

### ROR: Rotate right (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Rotate right" instruction to rotate the content of the operand at the IN input bit-by-bit to the right and query the result at the OUT output. You use the N parameter to specify the number of bit positions by which the specified value is to be rotated. The bit positions freed by rotating are filled with the bit positions that are pushed out.

If the value at the parameter N is "0", the value at input IN is copied to the operand at output OUT.

If the value at the N parameter is greater than the number of available bit positions, the operand value at the IN input is still rotated by the specified number of bit positions.

The following figure shows how the content of an operand of the DWORD data type is rotated three bit positions to the right:

![Description](images/51498091275_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Rotate right" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | BYTE, WORD, DWORD, DINT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Value to be rotated |
| N | Input | BYTE, WORD, INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Number of bit positions by which the value is rotated |
| OUT | Output | BYTE, WORD, DWORD, DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Result of the instruction |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/30468524427_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | 1010 1010 0000 1111 0000 1111 0101 0101 |
| N | Tag_Number | 5 |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | 1010 1101 0101 0000 0111 1000 0111 1010 |

If operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the "Rotate right" instruction is executed. The content of operand "TagIn_Value" is rotated five bit positions to the right. The result is sent at the "TagOut_Value" output. If the instruction is executed without errors, the ENO enable output has the signal state "1" and the "TagOut" output is set.

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)
  
[Basics of the EN/ENO mechanism](Programming%20basics.md#basics-of-the-eneno-mechanism)

### ROL: Rotate left (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Rotate left" instruction to rotate the content of the operand at the IN input bit-by-bit to the left and query the result at the OUT output. You use the N parameter to specify the number of bit positions by which the specified value is to be rotated. The bit positions freed by rotating are filled with the bit positions that are pushed out.

If the value at the parameter N is "0", the value at input IN is copied to the operand at output OUT.

If the value at the N parameter is greater than the number of available bit positions, the operand value at the IN input is still rotated by the specified number of bit positions.

The following figure shows how the content of an operand of the DWORD data type is rotated three bit positions to the left:

![Description](images/51500851211_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Rotate left" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | BYTE, WORD, DWORD, DINT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Value to be rotated |
| N | Input | BYTE, WORD, INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Number of bit positions by which the value is rotated |
| OUT | Output | BYTE, WORD, DWORD, DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Result of the instruction |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/30469404811_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameters | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | TagIn_Value | 1111 0000 1010 1010 0000 1111 0000 1111 |
| N | Tag_Number | 5 |
| OUT | TagOut_Value | 0001 0101 0100 0001 1110 0001 1111 1110 |

If the "TagIn" input has the signal state "1", the "Rotate left" instruction is executed. The content of operand "TagIn_Value" is rotated five bit positions to the left. The result is sent at the "TagOut_Value" output. If the instruction is executed without errors, the ENO enable output has the signal state "1" and the "TagOut" output is set.

### ---|   |---: Get status bit (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

With the "Get status bit" instruction you can query the signal state of the following status bits:

- BR: Binary result
- OV: Overflow
- OS: Latching overflow
- CC 0 and CC 1: Conditional codes

You define which status bits are queried by selecting the corresponding symbol from the drop-down list of the instruction. The following table shows the possible ways of querying status bits:

| Symbol | Query | Explanation |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ==0 | CC 0 = 0 and CC 1 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is equal to 0. |
| &lt;&gt;0 | CC 0 = 0 and CC 1 = 1   or  CC 0 = 0 and CC 1 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is not equal to 0. |
| &gt;=0 | CC 0 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is greater than or equal to 0. |
| &lt;=0 | CC 1 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is less than or equal to 0. |
| &gt;0 | CC 0 = 0 and CC 1 = 1 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is greater than 0. |
| &lt;0 | CC 0 = 1 and CC 1 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is less than 0. |
| UO | CC 0 = 1 and CC 1 = 1 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is invalid. The cause of an invalid result can be a floating-point number or division by zero. |
| OV | OV = 1 | The instruction queries whether a number range overflow has occurred. |
| OS | OS = 1 | The instruction queries whether a saving number range overflow has occurred. |
| BR | BR= 1 | The instruction asks the signal state of the status bit BR. |

The "Get status bit" instruction functions like a normally open contact. When the query is satisfied, the instruction has the signal state "1". If the query is not satisfied, the instruction has the signal state "0".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20238209163_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

If operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the "Multiply" (MUL) instruction is executed. In the event of an overflow during the execution of the "Multiply" instruction, the status bit OV is set. Following the query of the status bit OV, the "Set output" instruction (S) is executed in network 2 and the operand "TagOV" is set.

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting LAD elements](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#inserting-lad-elements)
  
[Editing LAD elements](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#editing-lad-elements)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

### ---| / |---: Get negated status bit (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

With the "Get negated status bit" instruction you can query the signal state of the following status bits and negate the query result:

- BR: Binary result
- OV: Overflow
- OS: Latching overflow
- CC 0 and CC 1: Conditional codes

You define which status bits are queried by selecting the corresponding symbol from the drop-down list of the instruction. The following table shows the possible ways of querying status bits:

| Symbol | Query | Explanation |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ==0 | CC 0 = 0 and CC 1 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is equal to 0. |
| &lt;&gt;0 | CC 0 = 0 and CC 1 = 1  or  CC 0 = 0 and CC 1 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is not equal to 0. |
| &gt;=0 | CC 0 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is greater than or equal to 0. |
| &lt;=0 | CC 1 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is less than or equal to 0. |
| &gt;0 | CC 0 = 0 and CC 1 = 1 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is greater than 0. |
| &lt;0 | CC 0 = 1 and CC 1 = 0 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is less than 0. |
| UO | CC 0 = 1 and CC 1 = 1 | The instruction asks whether the result of a mathematical function is invalid. The cause of an invalid result can be a floating-point number or division by zero. |
| OV | OV = 1 | The instruction asks whether a number range overflow has occurred. |
| OS | OS = 1 | The instruction asks whether a stored number range overflow has occurred in an instruction. |
| BR | BR= 1 | The instruction asks the signal state of the status bit BR. |

The "Get negated status bit" instruction functions like a normally closed contact. When the query is satisfied, the instruction has the signal state "0". If the query is not satisfied, the instruction has the signal state "1".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20253185163_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

If operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the "Multiply" (MUL) instruction is executed. If an overflow does not occur during the execution of the instruction, the status bit OV is reset to "0". Following the query of the status bit OV, the instruction "Set output" (S) is executed in network 2 and the operand "TagOut_2" is set.

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting LAD elements](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#inserting-lad-elements)
  
[Editing LAD elements](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#editing-lad-elements)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)

### ---(CALL): Call block (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Call block" instruction calls a function (FC) without parameter. The call is conditional or unconditional depending on the preceding logic operation.

In the statement part of a function (FC), you cannot specify any parameter of the BLOCK_FC data type as the operand for a conditional call. You can, however, specify a parameter of the type BLOCK_FC as the operand in a function block (FB).

A conditional call is then only executed if the result of logic operation (RLO) is "1". If a conditional call is not executed the RLO is "0" after the call operation. If the operation is executed, it works as follows:

- It stores the return address of the calling block.
- It stores the two data block registers (data block and instance data block).
- It updates the local data for the called function.
- It moves the MA bit (active MCR bit) to the block stack (B stack).

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Call block" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| &lt;Block&gt; | Output | BLOCK_FC | - | Called function |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/22497527179_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The function FC3 is called if the operand "TagIn_1" has the signal state "1".

---

**See also**

[Master control relay (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#master-control-relay-s7-300-s7-400-1)
  
[Important notes on using MCR functions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#important-notes-on-using-mcr-functions-s7-300-s7-400)
