### ---(SAVE): Save RLO in BR bit (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

Use the instruction "Save RLO in BR bit" to save the result of logic operation (RLO) in the binary result (BR). During processing, the instruction transfers the signal state of the current RLO to the status bit BR. The instruction operates independent of the conditions and does not affect any other status bits.

> **Note**
>
> After application of the instruction "Save RLO in BR bit", the BR bit can be modified again by the following instructions in the same or lower-level blocks.

Use the instruction "Save RLO in BR bit" to check the execution status of a block. If you program the instruction "Save RLO in BR bit" at the end of a block, for example, the BR bit is set to the signal state of the current result of logic operation of the block. If the block is executed without errors, the BR bit and the enable output ENO in the calling block are set to signal state "1". Signal state "0" is assigned to the BR bit if an error occurs during processing of the block. You can program a troubleshooting routine by querying the BR bit.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/11927593483_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The BR bit is set to the signal state "1" if one of the following conditions is met:

- The operands "TagIn_1" and "TagIn_2" have signal state "1".
- The operand "TagIn_3" has the signal state "1".

---

**See also**

[Basic information on the status word (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#basic-information-on-the-status-word-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Inserting LAD elements](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#inserting-lad-elements)
  
[Editing LAD elements](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#editing-lad-elements)
  
[Setting status bits (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#setting-status-bits-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Example of the use of the EN/ENO mechanism in LAD](Programming%20basics.md#example-of-the-use-of-the-eneno-mechanism-in-lad)

### ---(MCR<): Open MCR ranges (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Open MCR ranges" instruction saves the result of logic operation (RLO) in the MCR stack and enables MCR dependency within an MCR range (MCR = Master Control Relay).

The MCR stack can contain up to a maximum of 8 entries and functions like a LIFO buffer (Last In, First Out). When the stack is full, the instruction generates an error message (MCRF).

> **Note**
>
> Read the information on using MCR functions in the "Important notes on using MCR functionality" at "See also".

Use the instructions "Enable MCR range" (MCRA) and "Disable MCR range" (MCRD) to specify the start and end of an MCR range. Within the defined MCR range you can enable and disable MCR dependency for one or more program sections.

MCR dependency is enabled when the RLO is "1" before processing of the instruction. If the RLO is "0" before the instruction, MCR dependency is disabled. The end of the MCR dependent program section is programmed using the instruction "Close MCR ranges". The program section between the two instructions is affected by the MCR. Only the following MCR-dependent instructions are affected by this:

- Assignment
- Set output (S)
- Reset output (R)
- Reset/set flip-flop (RS)
- Set/reset flip-flop (SR)
- Move value (MOVE)

You can also nest the enabling and disabling of MCR dependency by programming the instruction "Open MCR ranges" in an MCR dependent program section. You can nest the instruction up to 8 levels deep. The MCR dependency of the higher-level program section hereby controls the MCR dependencies in all lower-level program sections. If MCR dependency is disabled in the higher-level program section, this MCR dependency cannot be switched on in any of the lower-level MCR dependent program sections.

If you call a block within an MCR range, MCR dependency is disabled in the called block. When the block is exited, MCR dependency is set so that it is the same as before the block call.

The instructions "Open MCR ranges" and "Close MCR ranges" must always be programmed in pairs. If one of the two instructions is not programmed, an MCR stack error is triggered.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/11927618699_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

The start of the MCR range is programmed in network 1. If the "TagIn_1" operand returns signal state "1", MCR dependency is enabled in the first level of the MCR range. In this case, the signal state of the "TagIn_4" operand is assigned to the "TagOut_2" operand (network 6). If the "TagIn_1" operand returns signal state "0", MCR dependency is disabled and the "TagOut_2" operand is reset to "0". MCR dependency of the MCR range is disabled in network 7.

In network 3, MCR dependency is enabled in the second level of the MCR range, when the "TagIn_2" operand has signal state "1" and the first level of the MCR range is enabled. In this case, the signal state of the "TagIn_3" operand is assigned to the "TagOut_1" operand. If the "TagIn_2" operand returns signal state "0", MCR dependency is disabled and the "TagOut_1" operand is reset to "0". MCR dependency in the second level of the MCR range is disabled in network 5. The end of the MCR range is programmed in network 8.

---

**See also**

[Important notes on using MCR functions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#important-notes-on-using-mcr-functions-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[Master control relay (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#master-control-relay-s7-300-s7-400-1)
  
[---(MCR&gt;): Close MCR ranges (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcr-close-mcr-ranges-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[---(MCRA): Enable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcra-enable-mcr-range-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[---(MCRD): Disable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcrd-disable-mcr-range-s7-300-s7-400)

### ---(MCR>): Close MCR ranges (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Close MCR ranges" completes an MCR dependent (MCR = Master Control Relay) program section. In this case the instruction deletes the result of logic operation (RLO) from the last entry in the MCR stack.

The MCR stack can contain up to a maximum of 8 entries and functions like a LIFO buffer (Last In, First Out). If the stack is already empty, the instruction generates an error message (MCRF).

> **Note**
>
> Read the information on using MCR functions in the "Important notes on using MCR functionality" at "See also".

Use the instruction "Open MCR ranges" to program MCR dependency. The instructions "Open MCR ranges" and "Close MCR ranges" must always be programmed in pairs. If one of the two instructions is not programmed, an MCR stack error is triggered.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/11927631115_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

The start of the MCR range is programmed in network 1. If the "TagIn_1" operand returns signal state "1", MCR dependency is enabled in the first level of the MCR range. In this case, the signal state of the "TagIn_4" operand is assigned to the "TagOut_2" operand (network 6). If the "TagIn_1" operand returns signal state "0", MCR dependency is disabled and the "TagOut_2" operand is reset to "0". MCR dependency of the MCR range is disabled in network 7.

In network 3, the MCR-dependency is enabled in the second level of the MCR range, when the "TagIn_2" operand has signal state "1". In this case, the signal state of the "TagIn_3" operand is assigned to the "TagOut_1" operand. If the "TagIn_2" operand returns signal state "0", the MCR dependency is disabled and the "TagOut_1" operand is reset to "0" regardless of the signal state of the "TagIn_3" operand. MCR dependency in the second level of the MCR range is disabled in network 5. The end of the MCR range is programmed in network 8.

---

**See also**

[Master control relay (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#master-control-relay-s7-300-s7-400-1)
  
[Important notes on using MCR functions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#important-notes-on-using-mcr-functions-s7-300-s7-400)

[---(MCRD): Disable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcrd-disable-mcr-range-s7-300-s7-400)

### ---(MCRA): Enable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

Use the instruction "Enable MCR range" to specify the start of an MCR range. Within this range, you can switch MCR dependency on and off using the following instructions:

- ---(MCR&lt;): Open MCR ranges
- ---(MCR&gt;): Close MCR ranges

You specify the end of the MCR range with the instruction "Disable MCR range" (MCRD). The instructions for defining the start and the end of an MCR range must always be used in pairs.

> **Note**
>
> Read the information on using MCR functions in the "Important notes on using MCR functionality" at "See also".

If you call a block within an MCR range, MCR dependency is disabled in the called block. When a block is exited, the MCR dependency is set so that it is the same as before the block call.

The instruction is executed regardless of the status bits and without affecting these bits.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/11927656331_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

The start of the MCR range is programmed in network 1. If the "TagIn_1" operand returns the signal state "1", the MCR dependency is enabled. In this case, the signal state of the "TagIn_2" operand is assigned to the "TagOut" operand (network 3). If the "TagIn_1" operand returns signal state "0", the MCR dependency is disabled and the "TagOut" operand is reset to "0" regardless of the signal state of the "TagIn_2" operand. MCR dependency of the MCR range is disabled in network 4. The end of the MCR range is programmed in network 8.

---

**See also**

[Master control relay (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#master-control-relay-s7-300-s7-400-1)
  
[Important notes on using MCR functions (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#important-notes-on-using-mcr-functions-s7-300-s7-400)

[---(MCR&gt;): Close MCR ranges (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcr-close-mcr-ranges-s7-300-s7-400)
  
[---(MCRD): Disable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcrd-disable-mcr-range-s7-300-s7-400)

### ---(MCRD): Disable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

Use the instruction "Disable MCR range" to specify the end of an MCR range.

You specify the start of the MCR range with the instruction "Enable MCR range" (MCRA). The instructions for defining the start and the end of an MCR range must always be used in pairs.

> **Note**
>
> Read the information on using MCR functions in the "Important notes on using MCR functionality" at "See also".

Within an MCR range you can program the MCR dependency with the help of the following instructions:

- ---(MCR&lt;): Open MCR ranges
- ---(MCR&gt;): Close MCR ranges

If you call a block within an MCR range, MCR dependency is disabled in the called block. When a block is exited, the MCR dependency is set so that it is the same as before the block call.

The instruction is executed regardless of the status bits and without affecting these bits.

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/11927681803_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-en-US.png)

The start of the MCR range is programmed in network 1. If the "TagIn_1" operand returns the signal state "1", the MCR dependency is enabled. In this case, the signal state of the "TagIn_2" operand is assigned to the "TagOut" operand (network 3). If the "TagIn_1" operand returns signal state "0", the MCR dependency is disabled and the "TagOut" operand is reset to "0" regardless of the signal state of the "TagIn_2" operand. MCR dependency of the MCR range is disabled in network 4. The end of the MCR range is programmed in network 8.

---

**See also**

[Master control relay (S7-300, S7-400)](Program%20flow%20control.md#master-control-relay-s7-300-s7-400-1)

[---(MCRA): Enable MCR range (S7-300, S7-400)](#mcra-enable-mcr-range-s7-300-s7-400)

### SET: Set bit array (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Set bit array" instruction sets the signal state of the bit in a specified area to "1". You use the pointer on the S_BIT parameter to define the starting point of the range. If the pointer points to the memory area of the external I/O, the instruction is not executed. At the N parameter, you specify the number of bits to be set in the specified area. When the N parameter has the value "0", calling the instruction has no effect.

The instruction is only executed when the MCR bit is "1". When the MCR bit has the signal state "0", the bits in the specified range are not changed.

> **Note**
>
> **Parameter N**
>
> You can also interconnect an element of a data block at parameter N.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Set bit array" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| S_BIT | Input | POINTER | I, Q, M, D | Pointer to the first bit of the range whose bits are set.  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Number of bits to be set |

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/43504859147_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the TagIn operand has the signal state "1", the instruction sets 10 bits in the area from M0.0 to M1.2.

---

[Inserting operands into LAD instructions](Creating%20LAD%20programs.md#inserting-operands-into-lad-instructions)

### SETP: Set a bit array in the I/O area (S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Set a bit array in the I/O area" sets the bits of an I/O area to the signal state "1". At the same time the corresponding bits in the process image of the outputs are also set parallel to the I/O bits.

You use the N and SA parameters of the instruction to define the bit array that will be set. The bits of the array must be located in the part of the I/O area to which a process image is assigned.

If no I/O devices are plugged in for part of the selected bit array, the instruction attempts to set the entire bit array. In this case an error information is output on the RET_VAL parameter.

The I/O area is set byte-by-byte. If the bit array defined via the N and SA parameters does not begin or end at a byte boundary, calling the instruction has the following effect:

- The bits that are in the first or last byte to be transferred and that do not belong to the defined bit array, get the value of the corresponding bits in the process image output.

  | Symbol | Meaning |
  | --- | --- |
  |  | **Warning** |
  | **Unintended behavior**  The setting of the bits to the value of the associated bits in the process image output can lead to unintended reactions such as starting a motor or turning off a cooling system. |  |
- The bits belonging to the defined bit array are set to the signal state "1".

The instruction "Set a bit array in the I/O area" must be called in an MCR area.

Calling the "Set a bit array in the I/O area" instruction has no effect and the enable output ENO is set to "0" if one of the following conditions applies:

- The EN enable input has the signal state "0".
- The N parameter has the value "0"
- The MCR bit has the signal state "1".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Set a bit array in the I/O area" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Number of bits to be set |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | Error information |
| SA | Output | POINTER | P | Pointer to the first bit to be set |

#### Parameter RET_VAL

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 8xyy | For more information on errors, refer to "See also". |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats under "See also". |  |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/24474241291_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the instruction sets 8 bits in the I/O range corresponding to the outputs Q10.0 to Q10.7.

### SETI: Set byte array (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Set byte array" instruction sets the signal state of the bit in a specified area of bytes to "1". You define the start point of the array on the S_BYTE. You define the size of the array by specifying the number of bits to be set on the N parameter of the instruction.

> **Note**
>
> The value of the N parameter must be a multiple of the number eight (for example, 8, 16, 24, etc.).

The pointer specified on the S_BYTE parameter must reference the external I/O memory area (P). Since the "I/0" memory area is accessed as bytes, words, or double words, the pointer on the S_BYTE parameter must reference an operand that corresponds to a byte limit value, in other words the bit number of the pointer must be "0".

> **Note**
>
> The signal state of the corresponding bits in the process-image output is reset to "0".

Calling the "Set byte array" instruction has no effect and the ENO enable output is set to "0" if one of the following conditions applies:

- The EN enable input has the signal state "0".
- The pointer on the S_BYTE parameter does not reference the external I/O memory area.
- The pointer on the S_BYTE parameter references an operand that is not byte-aligned.
- The value of the N parameter is not a multiple of the number 8.
- The MCR bit has the signal state "0".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Set byte array" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| S_BYTE | Input | POINTER | P or constant | Pointer to the first byte of the array whose bits are to be set.  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Size of the array to be set  The array is specified by the number of bits as a multiple of eight (for example 8, 16, 24 etc.). |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/43505019915_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the instruction sets 2 bytes (16 bits) in the range from P2.0 to P3.7.

---

### RESET: Reset bit array (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use"Reset bit array" instruction to reset the signal state of the bits in a specified area to "0". You use the pointer on the S_BIT parameter to define the starting point of the range. If the pointer points to the memory area of the external I/O, the instruction is not executed. You specify the number of bits to be reset in the specified range at the N parameter of the instruction. When the N parameter has the value "0", calling the instruction has no effect.

The instruction is only executed when the MCR bit is "1". When the MCR bit has the signal state "0", the bits in the specified range are not changed.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Reset bit array" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| S_BIT | Input | POINTER | I, Q, M, D | Pointer to the first bit of the range whose bits are to be reset  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Number of bits to be reset. |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20576167435_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the instruction resets 10 bits in the range from M0.0 to M1.2.

### RESETP: Reset a bit array in the I/O area (S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Reset a bit array in the I/O area" sets the bits of an I/O area to the signal state "0". At the same time the corresponding bits in the process image of the outputs are also reset parallel to the I/O bits.

You use the N and SA parameters to define the bit array that will be reset. The bits of the array must be located in the part of the I/O area to which a process image is assigned.

If no I/O devices are plugged in for part of the selected bit array, the instruction attempts to set the entire bit array. In this case an error information is output on the RET_VAL parameter.

The I/O area is reset byte-by-byte. If the bit array defined via the N and SA parameters does not begin or end at a byte boundary, calling the instruction has the following effect:

- The bits that are in the first and last bytes to be transferred and that do not belong to the defined bit array, get the value of the corresponding bits in the process image output table.

  | Symbol | Meaning |
  | --- | --- |
  |  | **Warning** |
  | **Unintended behavior**  The setting of the bits at the value of the relevant bit in the process image output table can lead, for example, to unintended reactions such as starting a motor or turning off a cooling system. |  |
- The bits belonging to the defined bit array are reset to the signal state "0".

The "Reset a bit array in the I/O area" instruction must be called in an MCR range.

Calling the "Reset a bit array in the I/O area" instruction has no effect and the enable output ENO is set to "0" if one of the following conditions applies:

- The EN enable input has the signal state "0".
- The N parameter has the value "0"
- The MCR bit has the signal state "1".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Reset a bit array in the I/O area" instruction:

| Parameters | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| N | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Number of bits to be reset. |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | Error information |
| SA | Output | POINTER | P | Pointer to the first bit to be reset. |

#### Parameter RET_VAL

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 8xyy | For more information on errors, refer to "See also". |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats under "See also". |  |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20576203787_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the operand "TagIn" has the signal state "1", the instruction sets 8 bits in the I/O range corresponding to the outputs Q10.0 to Q10.7.

### RESETI: Reset byte array (S7-300, S7-400)

The "Reset byte array" instruction is used to reset the signal state of the bits in a specified range of bytes to "0". Since the "I/0" memory area is accessed as bytes, words, or double words, the pointer on the S_BYTE parameter must reference an operand that corresponds to a byte limit value, in other words the bit number of the pointer must be "0".

> **Note**

### REPL_VAL: Enter substitute value (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

Use the "Enter substitute value" instruction to enter a substitute value in accumulator 1 (ACCU 1) from a synchronous error organization block of the program level causing the error.

> **Note**
>
> You can only call the "Enter substitute value" instruction in a synchronous error organization block (OB 121, OB 122).

Use the "Enter substitute value" instruction when you can no longer read any value from a module. The OB 122 is started after each access to this module. By calling the "Enter substitute value" instruction you can have the substitute value loaded in accumulator 1 of the interrupted program level. The program execution is then continued with this substitute value. The information needed for selecting the substitute value (for example, the block in which the error occurred or the address affected) is located in the local tags of OB 122.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Enter substitute value" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| VAL | Input | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Substitute value |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L | Error information |

#### Parameter RET_VAL

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the RET_VAL parameter:

| Error code*  (W#16#...) | Description |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 8080 | The instruction was not called from a synchronous error OB. |
| 8xyy | For additional information on errors, refer to "See also". |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats under "See also". |  |

---

**See also**

[Overview of the valid data types](Data%20types.md#overview-of-the-valid-data-types)

### DRUM: Implement sequencer (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Implement sequencer" instruction is used to assign the programmed values of the OUT_VAL parameter of the corresponding step to the programmed output bits (OUT1 to OUT16) and the output word OUT_WORD. The specific step must thereby satisfy the conditions of the programmed enable mask on the S_MASK parameter while the instruction remains at this step. The instruction advances to the next step if the event for the step is true and the programmed time for the current step elapses, or if the value at the JOG parameter changes from "0" to "1". The instruction is reset if the signal state on the RESET parameter changes to "1". The current step is hereby equated to the preset step (DSP).

The amount of time spent on a step is determined by the product of the preset timebase (DTBP) and the preset counter value (S_PRESET) for each step. At the start of a new step, this calculated value is loaded into the DCC parameter, which contains the time remaining for the current step. If, for example the value at the DTBP parameter is "2" and the preset value for the first step is "100" (100 ms), the DCC parameter has the value "200" (200 ms).

A step can be programmed with a timer value, an event, or both. Steps that have an event bit and the timer value "0" advance to the next step as soon as the signal state of the event bit is "1". Steps that are programmed only with a timer value start the time immediately. Steps that are programmed with an event bit and a timer value greater than "0" start the time when the signal state of the event bit is "1". The event bits are initialized with a signal state of "1".

When the sequencer is on the last programmed step (LST_STEP) and the time for this step has expired, the signal state on the Q parameter is set to "1"; otherwise it is set to "0". When the Q parameter is set, the instruction remains on the step until it is reset.

In the configurable mask (S_MASK), you can select the individual bits in the output word (OUT_WORD) and set or reset the output bits (OUT1 to OUT16) by means of the output values (OUT_VAL). If a bit of the configurable mask has signal state "1", the OUT_VAL value sets or resets the corresponding bit. If the signal state of a bit of the configurable mask is "0", the corresponding bit is left unchanged. All the bits of the configurable mask for all 16 steps are initialized with a signal state of "1".

The output bit at the OUT1 parameter corresponds to the least significant bit of the output word (OUT_WORD). The output bit at the OUT16 parameter corresponds to the most significant bit of the output word (OUT_WORD).

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, it is saved to the "Program resources" folder in the "Program blocks &gt; System blocks" path of the project tree. For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Implement sequencer" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| RESET | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" indicates the reset condition. |
| JOG | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | When the signal state changes from "0" to "1", the instruction advances to the next step. |
| DRUM_EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" causes the sequencer to advance based on the event and time criteria. |
| LST_STEP | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Number of the last programmed step. |
| EVENT(i),  1 ≤ i ≤ 16 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Event bit (i);  Initial signal state is "1". |
| OUT(j),  1 ≤ j ≤ 16 | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Output bit (j) |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" indicates that the time for the last step has elapsed. |
| OUT_WORD | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Word address to which the sequencer writes the output values. |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| JOG_HIS | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | JOG parameter history bit |
| EOD | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" indicates that the time for the last step has elapsed. |
| DSP | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Preset step of the sequencer |
| DSC | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Current step of the sequencer |
| DCC | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Current numerical value of the sequencer |
| DTBP | Static | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Preset timebase of the sequencer |
| PrevTime | Static | TIME | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Previous system time |
| S_PRESET | Static | ARRAY[1..16] of WORD | I, Q, M, D, L | Preset count for each step [1 to 16]; where 1 clock pulse = 1 ms. |
| OUT_VAL | Static | ARRAY[1..16, 0..15] of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Output values for each step [1 to 16, 0 to 15]. |
| S_MASK | Static | ARRAY[1..16, 0..15] of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Configurable mask for each step [1 to 16, 0 to 15]. Initial signal states are "1". |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Parameter ERR_CODE

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| ERR_CODE* | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| W#16#0000 | No error |
| W#16#000B | The value at the LST_STEP parameter is less than 1 or greater than 16. |
| W#16#000C | The value at the DSC parameter is less than 1 or greater than the value of the LST_STEP parameter. |
| W#16#000D | The value at the DSP parameter is less than 1 or greater than the value of the LST_STEP parameter. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

#### Example

In the following example the instruction advances from step 1 to step 2. The output bits (OUT1 to OUT16) and the output word (OUT_WORD) are set according to the mask configured for step 2 and the values of the OUT_VAL parameter.

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

![Example](images/68010054283_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

#### Before processing

In this example, the following values are used for initializing the input parameters:

| Parameter | Operand | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| RESET | Tag_Reset | M0.0 | FALSE |
| JOG | Tag_Input_JOG | M0.1 | FALSE |
| DRUM_EN | Tag_Input_Drum_EN | M0.2 | TRUE |
| LST_STEP | Tag_Number_LastStep | MB1 | B#16#08 |
| EVENT2 | MyTag_Event_2 | M20.0 | FALSE |
| EVENT4 | MyTag_Event_4 | M20.1 | FALSE |
| EVENT6 | MyTag_Event_6 | M20.2 | FALSE |
| EVENT8 | MyTag_Event_8 | M20.3 | FALSE |
| EVENT10 | MyTag_Event_10 | M20.4 | FALSE |
| EVENT12 | MyTag_Event_12 | M20.5 | FALSE |
| EVENT14 | MyTag_Event_14 | M20.6 | FALSE |
| EVENT16 | MyTag_Event_16 | M20.7 | FALSE |

The following values are saved in the "DRUM_DB" instance data block of the instruction:

| Parameter | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| JOG_HIS | DBX12.0 | FALSE |
| EOD | DBX12.1 | FALSE |
| DSP | DBB13 | W#16#0001 |
| DSC | DBB14 | W#16#0001 |
| DCC | DBD16 | DW#16#0000000A |
| DTBP | DBW20 | W#16#0001 |
| S_PRESET[1] | DBW26 | W#16#0064 |
| S_PRESET[2] | DBW28 | W#16#00C8 |
| OUT_VAL[1,0] | DBX58.0 | TRUE |

### DRUM_X: Implement sequencer (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Implement sequencer" instruction is used to implement a sequencer with maximum 16 steps. You specify the number of the first step on the DSP parameter. You specify the number of the last step on the LST_STEP parameter.

During each step, all 16 output bits OUT0 to OUT15 and the output parameter OUT_WORD (in which the output bits are collected together) are written. An output bit is assigned either the corresponding bit of the OUT_VAL array that you specified or the output bit of the preceding step. The value assigned depends on the value of the mask bit on the S_MASK parameter.

> **Note**
>
> The default setting for the mask bit is 0. If you want to change the current setting of one or more mask bits, make this change in the instance data block.

The "Implement sequencer" instruction advances to the next step when there is a rising edge on the JOG parameter. If the instruction is already in the last step, the tags Q and EOD are set when the JOG parameter has a rising edge. In this case the DCC parameter is set to the value "0". The instruction remains in the last step until the RESET parameter is set to the value "1".

You can also assign parameters so that switching to the next step is time dependent. To do this, the DRUM_EN parameter has to be set to the value "1". The transition to the next step is made when the event bit (EVENTi) belonging to the current step is set and the time specified for the current step has expired. The time for a step is the product of the (DTBP) time base and the time factor valid for the current step (S_PRESET).

> **Note**
>
> The execution time (DCC) remaining in the current step is reduced only when the corresponding event bit (EVENTi) is set.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multi-instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, it is saved to the "Program resources" folder in the "Program blocks &gt; System blocks" path of the project tree. For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

If the value "1" is set on the RESET parameter when the instruction is called, the sequencer goes to the step whose number you assigned on the DSP parameter.

A step can be programmed with a timer value, an event, or both. Steps that have an event bit and the timer value "0" advance to the next step as soon as the signal state of the event bit is "1". Steps that are programmed only with a timer value start the time immediately. Steps that are programmed with an event bit and a timer value greater than "0" start the time when the signal state of the event bit is "1".

You can also move the next step at any time via the value at the JOG parameter.

When the instruction is called for the first time, you must set the value "1" on the RESET parameter.

When the sequencer is in the last step and the execution time specified for this step has expired, the parameters Q and EOD are set. The instruction remains in the last step until the RESET parameter changes to the value "1".

The instruction is executed only in the STARTUP and RUN modes.

The operating system resets the "Implement sequencer" instruction during a cold restart. During a warm restart, the instruction is not reset. If you want the "Implement sequencer" instruction to be initialized after a warm restart, you have to call the OB 100 with the value "1" on the RESET parameter.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Implement sequencer" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| RESET | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | The signal state "1" resets the sequencer. When the instruction is called for the first time, you have to set the value "1" on the RESET parameter. |
| JOG | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | A positive signal edge (compared to the last call) switches the sequencer to the next step if it is not yet in the last step. The next step is enabled depending on the value you assigned to the DRUM_EN parameter. |
| DRUM_EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Control parameter that specifies whether time-dependent switching to the next step is possible. If the value is "1" a time-dependent switching to the next step is possible. |
| LST_STEP | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Number of the last step  Values from 1 to 16 are permitted. |
| EVENTi,  1 ≤ i ≤ 16 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Event bit number i (belongs to step i) |
| OUTj,  0 ≤ j ≤ 15 | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Output bit number j (identical to the bit number j j of OUT_WORD) |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Status parameter that indicates whether the specified execution time of the last step has expired. |
| OUT_WORD | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Output bits collected together in a tag |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| JOG_HIS | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Not relevant to user (input parameter JOG of the preceding call) |
| EOD | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Identical to the output parameter Q |
| DSP | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Number of the first step  Values from 1 to 16 are permitted. |
| DSC | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Number of the current step |
| DCC | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | The execution time still remaining in the current step in milliseconds (ms) (only relevant if DRUM_EN = 1 and the corresponding event bit = 1) |
| DTBP | Static | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | The time base valid for all steps in milliseconds (ms) |
| PREV_TIME | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | (Not relevant for the user: system time of the previous call) |
| S_PRESET | Static | ARRAY of WORD | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | One-dimensional array with the time factor for each step.  Recommended selection of the indices: [1 to 16].  In this case, S_PRESET [x] has the time factor of step x. |
| OUT_VAL | Static | ARRAY of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Two-dimensional array with the values to be output in each step if they have not been masked out using S_MASK.  Recommended selection of the indices: [1 to 16, 0 to 15]. In this case, OUT_VAL [x, y] has the value assigned to the output bit OUTy in step x. |
| S_MASK | Static | ARRAY of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Two-dimensional array with the mask bits for each step.  Recommended selection of the indices: [1 to 16, 0 to 15]. In this case, S_MASK [x, y] contains the mask bit for the "y"-th value output in step x.  Meaning of the mask bits:  - 0: The corresponding value of the previous step is assigned to the relevant output bit. - 1: The corresponding value from OUT_VAL is assigned to the relevant output bit. |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Parameter ERR_CODE

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| ERR_CODE* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 8081 | Invalid value at parameter LST_STEP. |
| 8082 | Invalid value on parameter DSC. |
| 8083 | Invalid value on parameter DSP. |
| 8084 | The product DCC = DTBP * S_PRESET[DSC] exceeds the value 2**31-1 (approximately 24.86 days). |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

### DCAT: Discrete control-timer alarm (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You can use the "Discrete control-timer alarm" instruction to accumulate the time from the point at which theCMD parameter issued the command to open or close. The time is accumulated until the preset time (PT) is exceeded or the information is received that the device was opened or closed (O_FB or C_FB) within the specified time. If the preset time is exceeded before the information on the opening or closing of the device is received, the corresponding alarm is activated. If the signal state on the command input changes state before the preset time, the time is restarted.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

The "Discrete control-timer alarm" instruction has the following reactions to the input conditions:

- When the signal state of the CMD parameter changes from "0" to "1", the signal states of the parameters Q, CMD_HIS, ET, OA and CA are influenced as follows:

  - The parameters Q and CMD_HIS are set to "1".
  - The parameters ET, OA and CA are reset to "0".
- When the signal state on the parameter CMD changes from "1" to "0", the parameters Q, ET, OA, CA and CMD_HIS are reset to "0".
- When the signal state of the parameters CMD and CMD_HIS is "1" and the parameter O_FB is set to "0", the time difference (ms) since the last execution of the instruction is added to the value at the parameter ET. If the value of the parameter ET exceeds the value of the parameter PT, the signal state on the parameter OA is set to "1". If the value of the parameter ET does not exceed the value of the parameter PT, the signal state on the parameter OA is reset to "0". The value at the parameter CMD_HIS is reset to the value of the parameter CMD.
- If the signal state of the parameters CMD, CMD_HIS and O_FB are set to "1" and the parameter C_FB has the value "0", the signal state of the parameter OA is set to "0". The value of the parameter ET is set to the value of the parameter PT. If the signal state of the parameter O_FB changes to "0", the alarm is set the next time the instruction is executed. The value of the parameter CMD_HIS is set to the value of the parameter CMD.
- If the parameters CMD, CMD_HIS and C_FB have the value "0", the time difference (ms) since the last execution of the instruction is added to the value of the parameter ET. If the value of the parameter ET exceeds the value of the parameter PT, the signal state of the parameter CA is set to "1". If the value at the parameter PT is not exceeded, the parameter CA has the signal state "0". The value of the parameter CMD_HIS is set to the value of the parameter CMD.
- If the parameters CMD, CMD_HIS and O_FB have the signal state "0" and the parameter C_FB is set to "1", the parameter CA is set to "0". The value of the parameter ET is set to the value of the parameter PT. If the signal state of the parameter C_FB changes to "0", the alarm is set the next time the instruction is executed. The value of the parameter CMD_HIS is set to the value of the parameter CMD.
- If the parameters O_FB and C_FB simultaneously have the signal state "1", the signal states of both alarm outputs are set to "1".

The "Discrete control-timer alarm" instruction has no error information.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Discrete control-timer alarm" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| CMD | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | A signal state of "0" indicates a "close" command.  A signal state of "1" indicates an "open" command. |
| O_FB | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Feedback input when opening |
| C_FB | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Feedback input when closing |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Shows the status of the parameter CMD |
| OA | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Alarm output when opening |
| CA | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Alarm output when closing |
| ET | Static | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Currently elapsed time, where one clock pulse = 1 ms |
| PT | Static | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Preset timer value, where one clock pulse = 1 ms |
| PREV_TIME | Static | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L | Previous system time |
| CMD_HIS | Static | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | CMD history bit |

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### Example

In the following example the parameter CMD changes from "0" to "1". After the execution of the instruction the parameter Q is set to "1" and the two alarm outputs OA and CA have the signal state "0". The parameter CMD_HIS of the instance data block is set to the signal state "1" and the parameter ET is reset to "0".

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

![Example](images/20590469131_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

| --- | --- | --- |

| O_FB | Tag_Input_O_FB | FALSE |
| C_FB | Tag_Input_C_FB | FALSE |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | FALSE |
| OA | Tag_Output_OA | FALSE |
| CA | Tag_Output_CA | FALSE |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "DCAT_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameter | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ET | DBD4 | L#12 |
| PT | DBD8 | L#222 |
| CMD_HIS | DBX16.0 | FALSE |

**After processing**

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | TRUE |
| OA | Tag_Output_OA | FALSE |
| CA | Tag_Output_CA | FALSE |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "DCAT_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameter | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| ET | DBD4 | L#0 |
| CMD_HIS | DBX16.0 | TRUE |

### MCAT: Motor control-timer alarm (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Motor control-timer alarm" is used to accumulate the time from the point of time as of which one of the command inputs (open or close) is activated. The time is accumulated until the preset time is exceeded or the relevant feedback input indicates that the device has executed the requested operation within the specified time. If the preset time is exceeded before the feedback is received, the corresponding alarm is triggered.

#### Execution of the "Motor control-timer alarm" instruction

The following table shows the reactions of the instruction "Motor control-timer alarm" to the various input conditions:

| Input parameters |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  | Output parameters |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ET | O_HIS | C_HIS |  | O_CMD | C_CMD | S_CMD | O_FB | C_FB | OO | CO | OA | CA | ET | O_HIS | C_HIS | Q | Status |
| X | 1 | 1 |  | X | X | X | X | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 | PT | 0 | 0 | 0 | Alarm |
| X | X | X |  | X | X | X | 1 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 | PT | 0 | 0 | 0 | Alarm |
| X | X | X |  | X | X | 1 | X | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | Stop |
| X | X | X |  | 1 | 1 | X | X | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | Stop |
| X | 0 | X |  | 1 | 0 | 0 | X | X | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 1 | Start opening |
| &lt;PT | 1 | 0 |  | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | INC | 1 | 0 | 1 | Open |
| X | 1 | 0 |  | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | PT | 1 | 0 | 1 | Opened |
| &gt;=PT | 1 | 0 |  | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | PT | 1 | 0 | 0 | Opening alarm |
| X | X | 0 |  | 0 | 1 | 0 | X | X | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 1 | Start closing |
| &lt;PT | 0 | 1 |  | 0 | X | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | INC | 0 | 1 | 1 | Close |
| X | 0 | 1 |  | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | PT | 0 | 1 | 1 | Closed |
| &gt;=PT | 0 | 1 |  | 0 | X | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 | PT | 0 | 1 | 0 | Closing alarm |
| X | 0 | 0 |  | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | X | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | X | 0 | 0 | 1 | Stopped |
| Legend: |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| INC |  |  | Add the time difference (ms) since the last processing of the FB to ET |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| PT |  |  | PT is set to the same value as ET |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| X |  |  | Cannot be used |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| &lt;PT |  |  | ET &lt; PT |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| &gt;=PT |  |  | ET &gt;= PT |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| If the input parameters O_HIS and C_HIS both have the signal state "1", they are immediately set to signal state "0". In this case, the last row in the table (X) mentioned above is valid. Because it is therefore no longer possible to check whether the input parameters O_HIS and C_HIS have the signal state "1", the output parameters are set as follows in this case:   OO = FALSE  CO = FALSE  OA = FALSE  CA = FALSE  ET = PT  Q = TRUE |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

The "Motor control-timer alarm" instruction returns no error information.

### IMC: Compare input bits with the bits of a mask (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Compare input bits with the bits of a mask" is used to compare the signal state of up to 16 programmed input bits (IN_BIT0 to IN_BIT15) with the corresponding bits of a mask. Up to 16 steps with masks can be programmed. The value of the IN_BIT0 parameter is compared with the value of the mask CMP_VAL[x,0], with "x" indicating the step number. At the CMP_STEP parameter, you specify the step number of the mask that is used for the comparison. All programmed values are compared in the same manner. Unprogrammed input bits or unprogrammed bits of the mask have a default signal state FALSE.

If a match is found in the comparison, the signal state of the OUT parameter is set to "1". Otherwise the OUT parameter is set to "0".

If the value of CMP_STEP parameter is greater than 15, the instruction is not executed. An error message is output at the ERR_CODE parameter.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Compare input bits with the bits of a mask" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN_BIT0 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 0 to be compared with bit 0 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT1 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 1 to be compared with bit 1 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT2 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 2 to be compared with bit 2 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT3 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 3 to be compared with bit 3 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT4 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 4 to be compared with bit 4 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT5 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 5 to be compared with bit 5 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT6 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 6 to be compared with bit 6 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT7 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 7 to be compared with bit 7 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT8 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 8 to be compared with bit 8 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT9 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 9 to be compared with bit 9 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT10 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 10 to be compared with bit 10 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT11 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 11 to be compared with bit 11 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT12 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 12 to be compared with bit 12 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT13 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 13 to be compared with bit 13 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT14 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 14 to be compared with bit 14 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT15 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 15 to be compared with bit 15 of the mask. |
| CMP_STEP | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | The step number of the mask used for the comparison. |
| OUT | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | A signal state of "1" indicates that a match was found.  A signal state of "0" indicates that a match was found. |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| CMP_VAL | Static | ARRAY of BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Comparison masks [0 to 15, 0 to 15]: The first number of the index is the step number and the second number is the bit number of the mask. |

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 000A | The value at the CMP_STEP parameter is greater than 15. |
| * The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal values in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats under "See also". |  |

### SMC: Compare scan matrix (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Compare scan matrix" instruction is used to compare the signal state of up to 16 programmed input bits (IN_BIT0 to IN_BIT15) with the corresponding bits of the comparison masks for each step. Processing starts at step 1 and is continued until the last programmed step (LAST) or until a match is found. The input bit of the IN_BIT0 parameter is compared with the value of the mask CMP_VAL[x,0], with "x" indicating the step number. All programmed values are compared in the same manner. If a match is found the signal state of the OUT parameter is set to "1" and the step number with the matching mask is written in the OUT_STEP parameter. Unprogrammed input bits or unprogrammed bits of the mask have a default signal state FALSE. If several steps have a corresponding mask, only the the first match is specified at the OUT_STEP parameter. If no match is found, the signal state of the OUT parameter is set to "0". In this case the value at the OUT_STEP parameter is greater by "1" than the value at the LAST parameter.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Compare scan matrix" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN_BIT0 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 0 to be compared with bit 0 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT1 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 1 to be compared with bit 1 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT2 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 2 to be compared with bit 2 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT3 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 3 to be compared with bit 3 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT4 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 4 to be compared with bit 4 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT5 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 5 to be compared with bit 5 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT6 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 6 to be compared with bit 6 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT7 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 7 to be compared with bit 7 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT8 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 8 to be compared with bit 8 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT9 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 9 to be compared with bit 9 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT10 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 10 to be compared with bit 10 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT11 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 11 to be compared with bit 11 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT12 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 12 to be compared with bit 12 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT13 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 13 to be compared with bit 13 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT14 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 14 to be compared with bit 14 of the mask. |
| IN_BIT15 | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Input bit 15 to be compared with bit 15 of the mask. |
| OUT | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | A signal state of "1" indicates that a match was found.  A signal state of "0" indicates that no match was found. |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| OUT_STEP | Output | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Contains the step number with the matching mask, or the step number which is greater by "1" than the value at the LAST parameter, provided no match is found. |
| LAST | Static | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Specifies the step number of the last step to be scanned for a matching mask. |
| CMP_VAL | Static | ARRAY of WORD | I, Q, M, D, L | Comparison masks [0 to 15, 0 to 15]: The first number of the index is the step number and the second number is the bit number of the mask. |

You can find additional information on valid data types under "See also".

#### ERR_CODE parameter

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 000E | The value at the LAST parameter is greater than 15. |
| * The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal values in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats under "See also". |  |

### LEAD_LAG: Lead and lag algorithm  (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction is used to process signals with an analog tag. The gain value at the GAIN parameter must be greater than zero. The result of the instruction "Lead and lag algorithm" is calculated using the following equation:

![Description](images/49016018315_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction supplies plausible results only when processing is in fixed program cycles. The same units must be specified for the LD_TIME, LG_TIME, and SAMPLE_T parameters. At LG_TIME &gt; 4 + SAMPLE_T, the instruction approaches the following function:

OUT = GAIN * ((1 + LD_TIME * s) / (1 + LG_TIME * s)) * IN

When the value of the GAIN parameter is less than or equal to zero, the calculation is not performed and an error information is output on the ERR_CODE parameter.

You can use the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction in conjunction with loops as a compensator in dynamic feed-forward control. The instruction consists of two operations. The "Lead" operation shifts the phase of the OUT output so that the output leads the input. The "Lag" operation, on the other hand, shifts the output so that the output lags behind the input. Because the "Lag" operation is equivalent to an integration, it can be used as a noise suppressor or as a low-pass filter. The "Lead" operation is equivalent to a differentiation and can therefore be used as a high-pass filter. The two operations together (Lead and Lag) result in the output phase lagging behind the the input at lower frequencies and leading it at higher frequencies. This means that the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction can be used as a band pass filter.

When you insert the instruction in the program, the "Call options" dialog opens in which you can specify whether the block parameters will be stored in a separate data block (single instance) or as a local tag (multiple instance) in the block interface. If you create a separate data block, you will find it in the project tree in the "Program resources" folder under "Program blocks &gt; System blocks". For additional information on this topic, refer to "See also".

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Lead and lag algorithm" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | The input value of the current sample time (cycle time) to be processed.  Constants can also be specified on the IN parameter. |
| SAMPLE_T | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Sample time  Constants can also be specified on the SAMPLE_T parameter. |
| OUT | Output | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |
| ERR_CODE | Output | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Error information |
| LD_TIME | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Lead time in the same unit as sample time. |
| LG_TIME | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Lag time in in the same unit as sample time. |
| GAIN | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Gain as % / % (the ratio of the change in output to a change in input as a steady state). |
| PREV_IN | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Previous input |
| PREV_OUT | Static | REAL | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Previous output |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Parameter ERR_CODE

The following table shows the meaning of the values of the ERR_CODE parameter:

| Error code* (W#16#...) | Explanation |
| --- | --- |
| 0000 | No error |
| 0009 | The value at the GAIN parameter is less than or equal to zero. |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For additional information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

> **Note**
>
> You can initialize static parameters in the data block.

![Example](images/20590825483_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

**Before processing**

In this example the following values are used for the input parameters:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_Input | 2.0 |
| SAMPLE_T | Tag_InputSampleTime | 10 |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "LEAD_LAG_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameter | Address | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| LD_TIME | DBD12 | 2.0 |
| LG_TIME | DBD16 | 2.0 |
| GAIN | DBD20 | 1.0 |
| PREV_IN | DBD24 | 6.0 |
| PREV_OUT | DBD28 | 6.0 |

**After processing**

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| OUT | Tag_Output_Result | 2.0 |

The following values are saved in the instance data block "LEAD_LAD_DB" of the instruction:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| PREV_IN | DBD24 | 2.0 |
| PREV_OUT | DBD28 | 2.0 |

### TONR_X: Time accumulator (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

You use the "Time accumulator" instruction to accumulate time values within a period which you set using the PV input. The instruction is executed when the signal state on the TMR_EN start input changes from "0" to "1". Simultaneously, the timer runs for the duration set at the PV input. While the instruction is being executed, it adds the time value of the DELTA_T input to the time value of the InOut ET.

The following conditions must be met:

- The TMR_EN start input has the signal state "1".
- The time value at InOut ET is less than the time value at the PV parameter.
- The RESET input has the signal state "0".

The instruction is interrupted when the signal state on the TMR_EN start input changes from "1" to "0". As soon as the signal state changes back to "1", the instruction resumes execution.

The instruction is ended when the time value at InOut ET has reached the time value at the PV input. The Q output then has the signal state "1".

As long as the Q output has the signal state "1", the time value at InOut ET remains unchanged. The time value and the Q output are not reset to "0" until the RESET input is set to signal state "1".

Since the "Time accumulator" instruction uses the cycle time (DELTA_T) of the last cycle of the organization block (OB), the instruction may only be called in cyclic organization blocks.

> **Note**
>
> You have to move the cycle time of the organization block from the startup information to the global tag of the DELTA_T parameters.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Time accumulator" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Enable output |
| TMR_EN (Timer Enable) | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Start input  Starts the instruction and the expiration of the preset time duration at the PV input |
| RESET | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L, T, C | Reset input |
| PV (Preset Value) | Input | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L, P, or constant | Maximum duration of time recording |
| DELTA_T | Input | INT | I, Q, M, D, L or constant | Cycle time of organization block of the previous cycle |
| Q | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Output which is set when the preset time value is reached |
| ET (Elapsed Time) | InOut | DINT | I, Q, M, D, L | Accumulated time value  (Currently elapsed time value + time value of the DELTA_T input) |

For additional information on valid data types, refer to "See also".

#### Pulse diagram

The following figure shows the pulse timing diagram of the "Time accumulator" instruction:

![Pulse diagram](images/65905837067_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/65911149579_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

If the operands "TagIn" and "Tag_Start" have the signal state "1", the instruction is started. Each time the signal state changes from "0" to "1" at the TMR_EN input, the cycle time "2" at the DELTA_T input is added to the current time value of InOut ET until the maximum time value "10" of the PV input is reached. If the instruction is executed without errors, the ENO enable output has the signal state "1" and the "TagOut" output is set.

---

### WSR: Save data to shift register (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Save data to shift register" instruction is used to write a bit from a specified source to a shift register. Each element of the register is shifted into the next address. The data contained in the last address of the shift register is lost after the shift.

Each time the instruction is executed with the value "0" on the RESET parameter, new data are read from the source (S_DATA) and shifted to the start address (START) of the shift register. The LENGTH parameter specifies the number of elements to be shifted. You specify the data type of the elements on the E_TYPE parameter. The instruction is not executed if an invalid data type is specified on the E_TYPE parameter.

The register is deleted if the RESET parameter is set to "1" when the instruction is executed. The Q parameter is set to the signal state "1" when the shift register is filled with zeros or deleted.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Save data to shift register" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| RESET | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Reset input |
| S_DATA | Input | POINTER | I, Q, M, D | Points to the source data element to be shifted to the start address (START).  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| START | Input | POINTER | I, Q, M, D | Points to the start address of the register.  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| LEN | Input | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Number of elements to be shifted. |
| E_TYPE | Input | BYTE | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Specifies the data type of the elements to be shifted. The following data types are permitted:  - W#16#04 = WORD - B#16#05 = INT - B#16#06 = DWORD - B#16#07 = DINT - B#16#08 = REAL |
| Q | Output | BOOL | Q, M, D, L | Is set to "0" if RESET parameter is active (1) or all elements to be shifted have the value "0". |

#### Example

In the following example four elements of the data type WORD are shifted starting from the address specified on the START parameter. When the first element of the register has been shifted to the next address, the first address is filled with the data that the pointer references on the S_DATA parameter. The value of the last element in the register is lost in the process.

![Example](images/51559453067_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

**Before processing**

In this example, the following values are used for the input and output parameters:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| RESET | Tag_Input_Reset | 0 |
| S_DATA | Tag_Input_DataSource | P#DB2.DBX6.0  DW0 = W#16#1111  DW2 = W#16#2222  DW4 = W#16#3333  DW6 = W#16#4444 |
| START | Tag_Input_StartAddress | P#DB1.DBX0.0  DW6 = W#16#1234 |
| LEN | Tag_Input_Length | W#16#04 |
| E_TYPE | Tag_Input_ElementType | B#16#04 |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | 1 |

**After processing**

The following values are written to the output parameters after the instruction has been executed:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| RESET | Tag_Input_Reset | 0 |
| S_DATA | Tag_Input_DataSource | P#DB2.DBX6.0  DW0 = W#16#1234  DW2 = W#16#1111  DW4 = W#16#2222  DW6 = W#16#3333 |
| START | Tag_Input_StartAddress | P#DB1.DBX0.0  DW6 = W#16#1234 |
| LEN | Tag_Input_Length | W#16#04 |
| E_TYPE | Tag_Input_ElementType | B#16#04 |
| Q | Tag_Output_Q | 1 |

### SHRB: Shift bit to shift register (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Shift bit to shift register" instruction is used to write a bit from a specified source (DATA) to a shift register. Each time the instruction is executed with a value "0" on the RESET parameter, new data are read from the source and shifted to the start address (S_BIT) of the shift register. All following bits are shifted by one. The bit contained at the last address (S_BIT + N) is lost after the shift. If the RESET parameter is set to "1" during the processing of the instruction, the addresses in the shift register are reset to "0" and not shifted.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Shift bit to shift register" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| DATA | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Source bit |
| RESET | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Reset input |
| S_BIT | Input | POINTER | I, Q, M, D | Points to the start bit of the shift register  For area-crossing, indirect register addressing, the pointer must be specified in double-word format. |
| N | Input | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Number of bits to be shifted. |

#### Example

In the following example the N parameter is set to the value 14 ("E" in hexadecimal). As a result 14 bits starting from the address specified on the S_BIT parameter are shifted. After the bits have been shifted, the first address is filled with the data from the source on the DATA parameter. The last bit value is lost.

![Example](images/39697261579_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following tables show how the instruction works using specific values.

#### **Before processing**

In this example, the following values are used for the input and output parameters:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |
| --- | --- | --- |
| RESET | Tag_Input_Reset | 0 |
| DATA | Tag_Input_Data | 0 |
| S_BIT | Tag_Input_BitSource | P#DB1.DBX1.4 |
| N | Tag_Input_Number | B#16#0E |

Before processing the instruction the following signal states are stored in the 14 bits of the register:

![Before processing](images/17885167627_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

#### After processing

After the processing of the instruction the following signal states are stored in the 14 bits of the register:

![After processing](images/17887009419_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

### SEG: Create bit pattern for seven-segment display (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The instruction "Create bit pattern for seven-segment display" is used to convert each of the four hexadecimal digits of the specified source word (IN) into an equivalent bit pattern for a seven-segment display. The result of the instruction is output in the double word on the OUT parameter.

The following relation exists between the hexadecimal digits and the assignment of the 7 segments (a, b, c, d, e, f, g):

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| **Input digit**   (Binary) | **Assignment of the segments**    **‑ g f e d c b a** | **Display**   (Hexadecimal) | **Seven-segment display** |
| 0000 | 00111111 | 0 | ![Description](images/7307290891_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png) |
| 0001 | 00000110 | 1 |  |
| 0010 | 01011011 | 2 |  |
| 0011 | 01001111 | 3 |  |
| 0100 | 01100110 | 4 |  |
| 0101 | 01101101 | 5 |  |
| 0110 | 01111101 | 6 |  |
| 0111 | 00000111 | 7 |  |
| 1000 | 01111111 | 8 |  |
| 1001 | 01100111 | 9 |  |
| 1010 | 01110111 | A |  |
| 1011 | 01111100 | B |  |
| 1100 | 00111001 | C |  |
| 1101 | 01011110 | D |  |
| 1110 | 01111001 | E |  |
| 1111 | 01110001 | F |  |

#### Parameter

The following table shows the parameters of the "Create bit pattern for seven-segment display" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | WORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Source word with four hexadecimal digits |
| OUT | Output | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Bit pattern for the seven-segment display |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/39697460363_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction works using specific operand values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Hexadecimal | Binary |  |  |
| IN | Tag_Input | W#16#1234 | 0001 0010 0011 0100 |
| OUT | Tag_Output | DW#16065B4F66 | 000 00110 0101 1011 0100 1111 0110 0110  Display: 1234 |

### BCDCPL: Create tens complement (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Create tens complement" instruction is used to create the tens complement of a seven-digit BCD number specified by the IN parameter. This instruction uses the following mathematical formula to calculate:

10000000 (as BCD)

– 7-digit BCD value

----------------------------------------

Tens complement (as BCD)

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Create tens complement" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | 7-digit BCD number |
| ERR_CODE | Output | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Result of the instruction |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/41943031691_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction functions using specific values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value* |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_Input | DW#16#01234567 |
| ERR_CODE | Tag_Output | DW#16#08765433 |
| * The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal values in the program editor. You can find information on switching the display formats under "See also". |  |  |

### BITSUM: Count number of set bits (S7-300, S7-400)

#### Description

The "Count number of set bits" instruction is used to count the number of bits of an operand that is set to the signal state "1". The operand whose bits are to be counted is specified on the IN parameter. The result of the instruction is output on the RET_VAL parameter.

#### Parameters

The following table shows the parameters of the "Count number of set bits" instruction:

| Parameter | Declaration | Data type | Memory area | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| EN | Input | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable input |
| ENO | Output | BOOL | I, Q, M, D, L | Enable output |
| IN | Input | DWORD | I, Q, M, D, L, P or constant | Operand whose set bits are counted |
| RET_VAL | Output | INT | I, Q, M, D, L, P | Number of set bits |

#### Example

The following example shows how the instruction works:

![Example](images/20590902283_DV_resource.Stream@PNG-de-DE.png)

The following table shows how the instruction functions using specific values:

| Parameter | Operand | Value* |
| --- | --- | --- |
| IN | Tag_Input | DW#16#12345678 |
| RET_VAL | Tag_Output | W#16#000D (13 Bits) |
| *The error codes can be displayed as integer or hexadecimal value in the program editor. For additional information on toggling display formats, refer to "See also". |  |  |
